Basrans and Baghdadis on Divine Will and Vision
Refutation of Mu'tazili denial of divine will and Beatific Vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili denial of Allah's effective will and the Beatific Vision, and the evidence from Quran and Hadith refuting them.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila deny two core Sunni beliefs: Allah's all-encompassing will and the vision of Allah in the Hereafter.

Imam al-Baqillani confronts two related heterodox claims from the Basran and Baghdadi Mu'tazila: that Allah's will does not determine all events, and that the believers will not see Him in Paradise. These claims contradict explicit Quranic verses and authentic hadith. In this lesson, we examine the arguments and the evidence the author brings against them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims
Read the passage and note the two positions attributed to the Basrans and Baghdadis.
The first is about Allah's will, the second about seeing Him in the afterlife.
2
Understand the first claim
They claim Allah's will is ineffective, contradictory to the Muslim consensus: 'mā shā'a Allāh kāna'.
3
Understand the second claim
They deny the vision of Allah (ru'ya) in the Hereafter, except for a few.
4
Examine the proofs
The author cites Quran 75:22-23, 7:143, and the hadith of seeing Allah like the moon.
These are direct textual proofs for the Sunni position.
5
Reflect on the importance
Why are these beliefs fundamental to Sunni theology? Consider divine power and human hope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم البصريون والبغداديون أنه يكون في سلطانه ما يكرهه ولا يريده، وأنه يكون شاءه أم أباه، وأنه يريد أبداً ما لا يكون ويكون ما لا يريد ردّاً لما اتفق عليه المسلمون من أن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن . وقالوا جميعاً إلا من شدّ منهم إن الله تعالى لا يُرى في المعاد، ردّاً للقرآن وجحداً للسنن والآثار. قال الله تعالى : وجوه يومئذ ناضرة إلى ربها ناظرة وقال : فإن استقر مكانه فسوف تراني وقال النبيّ صلّى الله عليه : «ترون ربّكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر . وكيف بكم إذا رأيتم الله؟» في أخبار يطول ذكرها.
And the Basrans and Baghdadis claimed that there happens in His dominion what He dislikes and does not will, and that it happens whether He wills it or not, and that He eternally wills what does not occur and what does occur He does not will, in contradiction to what the Muslims agreed upon: that what Allah wills occurs, and what He does not will does not occur. And they all said, except for a few among them, that Allah, exalted, will not be seen in the Hereafter, as a rejection of the Quran and a denial of the prophetic traditions and reports. Allah Most High said: 'Faces on that day will be radiant, looking at their Lord.' And He said: 'But if it stays in its place, you will see Me.' And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'You will see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon.' And 'How will it be when you see Allah?' in reports too lengthy to mention.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage combines two related doctrines held by the Basran and Baghdadi Mu'tazila: (1) the denial of the effective will of Allah over all events—they claim that things Allah dislikes occur without His will, and that He often wills things that do not happen, directly contradicting the Sunni consensus expressed in the maxim 'mā shā'a Allāh kāna wa mā lam yasha' lam yakun' (what Allah wills occurs; what He does not will does not occur); (2) the denial of the Beatific Vision (ru'yat Allāh) in the Hereafter, which the author calls a rejection of the Quran and denial of prophetic traditions (sunan wa āthār). The author then provides three proofs for the Sunni position: Quran 75:22-23 ('وجوه يومئذ ناضرة إلى ربها ناظرة'), Quran 7:143 (the story of Moses asking to see Allah), and the famous hadith narrated by Bukhari that the believers will see Allah like they see the moon on a clear night. The author concludes by referencing numerous other reports.

Key Terms
البصريون
البغداديون
ما شاء الله كان
الرؤية
ناضرة إلى ربها ناظرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila outright deny Allah's sovereignty and the possibility of seeing Him.
Correction: The Mu'tazila reinterpret Allah's will to exclude evil actions and interpret Quranic 'nādhira' as 'waiting for reward' rather than seeing. They do not deny Allah's sovereignty per se, but restrict His will.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the author cite to prove the Beatific Vision?
A) وجوه يومئذ ناضرة إلى ربها ناظرة
B) لا تدركه الأبصار
C) ليس كمثله شيء
D) ولا يحيطون به علما

Key Takeaway
The Basran and Baghdadi Mu'tazila denied both Allah's all-encompassing will and the vision of Him in the Hereafter, but the Quran and Sunnah decisively affirm both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been in a situation where you felt something terrible happened that could not have been in Allah's will? How does this passage's affirmation that 'what Allah wills occurs, and what He does not will does not occur' challenge you to trust His decree even when you don't understand it? What one step can you take this week to strengthen your reliance on His will?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) promised the believers that they will see Allah like the moon on a full night. Do you truly yearn for that moment, or do other hopes distract your heart? If your desire to see your Lord is weak, what is holding you back, and what will you do today to revive that longing?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected clear scriptures out of intellectual pride. Where in your own life do you find yourself rationalizing away a clear command of Allah or His Messenger because it doesn't fit your preferences? Will you repent and submit to His word, even when it costs you?

Mu'tazila on al-Ṣalāḥ and Divine Power
Baqillani reports Mu'tazila doctrines on al-ṣalāḥ and finite power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila doctrine that God does the absolute best for His servants and how this implies a limitation on divine power.

Core Idea
God's power cannot be limited by obligation to do the best.

This passage from al-Baqillani's Tamhīd reports two key Mu'tazila positions on God's action. Both groups assert that God has done the utmost best for His servants, but they differ on whether this covers all affairs or only religious matters. The critical consequence is that they all conclude God's power is finite—He cannot do better or even the like. This directly challenges the Sunni belief in absolute divine omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the two groups mentioned and their claims.
The passage has some missing words, but the main ideas are clear.
2
Identify the two positions
Distinguish what the Baghdadis (with al-Naẓẓām) claim versus the Basrans specifically. Notice the scope: one includes both religious and worldly affairs, the other only religious.
3
Analyze the consequence
Both groups end up saying God's power is limited—He can do a best but cannot do its like or surpass it. Ask yourself: why is this problematic for Sunni theology?
This is the core doctrinal error Baqillani is highlighting.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Consider the common misunderstanding that this might seem to affirm God's goodness, but it actually restricts His power. The commentary explains why this contradicts Sunni belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم البغداديون منهم، والنظام من البصريين أيضاً، أن القديم سبحانه قد استصلح عباده بغاية ما يقدر عليه من الصلاح، وأنه ليس في خزائنه ولا في سلطانه ولا يُتوهّم منه صلاح يقدر عليه أكثر مما قد استصلحهم به في دينهم ودنياهم. وزعم البصريون منهم خاصةً أنه تعالى قد استصلح عباده بغاية ما [؟] خاصةً، وأنه لا يقدر على صلاح في [؟] قدرته من الصلاح في باب دينهم [؟] لهم في باب الدين أصلح مما فعله بهم فأوجبوا جميعاً تناهي مقدوراته، وأنه يقدر على صلاح لا يقدر على مثله ولا على الزيادة عليه
The Baghdadis among them, and al-Naẓẓām from the Basrans also, claimed that the Eternal (al-Qadīm), glory be to Him, has done the best for His servants to the utmost of what He is able of the best (al-ṣalāḥ), and that there is not in His treasuries nor in His dominion nor can it be imagined from Him a best that He is able to do more than what He has done for them in their religion and their worldly life. And the Basrans among them specifically claimed that He, exalted, has done the best for His servants to the utmost of what is [؟] specifically, and that He is not able to do a best in [؟] His power of the best in the matter of their religion [؟] for them in the matter of religion better than what He did for them. So they all necessitated the finitude of His power, and that He is able to do a best like which He is not able to do the like nor increase upon it.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage reports two Mu'tazila positions on God's action. The Baghdadis, along with al-Naẓẓām from Basra, assert that God has done the absolute best (al-ṣalāḥ) for His servants, covering both religious and worldly affairs, and that it is inconceivable for Him to do more. The Basrans specifically restrict this to religious matters, claiming that God cannot do better for them in religion than what He has done. Both groups conclude that God's power is finite—He can do a best but cannot surpass it or produce its equal. This doctrine limits divine omnipotence and contradicts Sunni belief in God's unlimited power.

Key Terms
القدم القديم (al-Qadīm)
الصلاح (al-ṣalāḥ)
تناهي المقدورات (tanāhī al-maqdūrāt)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God is obligated to do the best for His servants, and that this best exhausts His power.
Correction: Sunni theology affirms that God is not obligated to do anything, and His power is infinite—He can create better or equal whenever He wills.

Checkpoint
According to the Baghdad Mu'tazila, what did God do for His servants?
A) He punished them unjustly
B) He did the best to the utmost of His ability
C) He did nothing
D) He created evil

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila doctrine of al-ṣalāḥ leads to the conclusion that God's power is finite, which contradicts the Sunni belief in absolute divine omnipotence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardships or unanswered prayers, do you ever feel that God 'could have done better'? How does the Mu'tazila error of limiting God's power by your own standard of 'best' reveal a subtle lack of trust in His absolute wisdom and goodness?
?
What does it mean for your daily life that God's power is not constrained by any obligation, including the obligation to give you what you think is best? Are you willing to surrender your notions of 'best' to His unrestricted will?
?
The Basrans restricted 'the best' to religious matters. In your own life, do you tend to compartmentalize God's sovereignty – trusting Him for spiritual matters but doubting His control over your worldly affairs? What step can you take today to submit both domains to His unlimited power?

Mu'tazila on God's Will and What He Dislikes
Baqillani reports Mu'tazila view that what God dislikes occurs against His will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila position on divine will and how it contradicts the Sunni consensus on the efficacy of God's will.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila claimed that what God dislikes can still happen — undermining His sovereign will.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani reports a controversial doctrine of the Mu'tazila regarding God's will. They argued that events can occur in God's dominion that He dislikes and does not will, and that He wills things that never happen. This directly contradicts the well-known Sunni principle that everything that occurs is by Allah's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation to grasp the Mu'tazila claims.
Notice the structure: three distinct claims followed by the Sunni rebuttal.
2
Identify the three claims
The passage lists three specific assertions of the Mu'tazila. List them: (1) things He dislikes occur, (2) they happen whether He wills or not, (3) He wills what never occurs and what He does not will occurs.
3
Contrast with Sunni consensus
The passage ends with the Sunni reply: 'Whatever God wills occurs, and whatever He does not will does not occur.' Compare this with each Mu'tazila claim to see the direct opposition.
This highlights the core disagreement about God's effective will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم البصريون والبغداديون أنه يكون في سلطانه ما يكرهه ولا يريده، وأنه يكون شاءه أم أباه، وأنه يريد أبداً ما لا يكون ويكون ما لا يريد ردّاً لما اتفق عليه المسلمون من أن ما شاء الله كان وما لم يشأ لم يكن.
And the Basrans and Baghdadis claimed that there occurs in His dominion what He dislikes and does not will, and that it occurs whether He wills or refuses, and that He eternally wills what does not occur and there occurs what He does not will, in opposition to what the Muslims have agreed upon, that whatever God wills occurs and whatever He does not will does not occur.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage reports the Mu'tazila position on divine will. They claim that events can happen in God's dominion that He dislikes and does not will, and that such events occur regardless of His will. Furthermore, they assert that God eternally wills things that never happen, while things He does not will come to pass. Baqillani notes that this contradicts the Sunni consensus (ijmāʿ) expressed in the principle 'Whatever God wills occurs, and whatever He does not will does not occur.' The Mu'tazila are thus portrayed as opposing a core Sunni tenet about the efficacy of God's will.

Key Terms
يكره (yakrah)
يريد (yurīd)
ما شاء الله كان (mā shā'a Allāh kāna)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila denied that God has a will.
Correction: The Mu'tazila affirmed God's will, but they claimed that it does not necessarily correspond to what actually happens, which limits His effective control.

D) Everything that occurs is what God wills

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila held that God's will is not always effective, contradicting the Sunni principle that everything occurs by His will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you hold the Sunni belief that God's will is always effective, what concrete difference does it make in how you react to disappointments? Do you live as if God's will is truly in control, or do you still worry as if things can happen without His permission?

Mu'tazila Denial of Seeing God and Baqillani's Refutation
Baqillani cites Mu'tazila denial of ru'ya and refutes with Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazila position on ru'ya and how Baqillani refutes it using the Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila deny seeing God, but the Quran and hadith affirm it.

This lesson presents the Mu'tazila denial of the vision of God in the Hereafter, a key point of contention between them and the Ahl al-Sunna. Imam Baqillani cites two clear Quranic verses and a prophetic hadith to refute their position, showing that the denial contradicts revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation together. Let the author's own words present the Mu'tazila claim and the evidence before you analyze.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila claim
Notice that the Mu'tazila (except a few) assert that God is not seen in the Hereafter. Baqillani describes this as rejection of the Qur'an and Sunnah.
3
Examine the first Quranic evidence
Read the verse from Surah al-Qiyama (75:22-23): 'Faces on that Day are radiant, looking at their Lord.' Reflect on how this directly affirms vision of God.
The word 'nāẓira' implies seeing with the eyes.
4
Examine the second Quranic evidence
Read the verse from Surah al-A'raf (7:143), where Moses is told 'If it settles in its place, you will see Me.' This indicates the possibility of seeing God.
5
Reflect on the hadith evidence
Consider the hadith comparing seeing God to seeing the moon. This is a clear affirmation of ru'ya. Baqillani also mentions many similar reports.
The hadith is widely transmitted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا جميعاً إلا من شدّ منهم إن الله تعالى لا يُرى في المعاد، ردّاً للقرآن وجحداً للسنن والآثار. قال الله تعالى: ﴿وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ نَاضِرَةٌ * إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ﴾، وقال: ﴿فَإِنِ اسْتَقَرَّ مَكَانَهُ فَسَوْفَ تَرَانِي﴾. وقال النبيّ صلّى الله عليه وسلّم: «ترون ربّكم كما ترون القمر ليلة البدر». وكيف بكم إذا رأيتم الله؟ في أخبار يطول ذكرها.
And they all, except a few among them, said that God, exalted, is not seen in the Hereafter, in rejection of the Qur'an and denial of the Sunnas and traditions. God, exalted, said: 'Faces on that Day are radiant, looking at their Lord' (75:22-23). And He said: 'If it settles in its place, you will see Me' (7:143). And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'You will see your Lord as you see the moon on the night of the full moon.' And 'How will it be when you see God?' in reports whose mention would be lengthy.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage reports the Mu'tazila position on the vision of God (ru'ya) in the afterlife. Most of them deny that God can be seen, with only a few exceptions. Baqillani then refutes this by citing two Qur'anic verses: Surah al-Qiyama 75:22-23, which describes faces looking at their Lord, and Surah al-A'raf 7:143, where Moses is told he will see God if the mountain settles. He also cites a prophetic hadith comparing the vision of God to seeing the moon, and another hadith mentioning seeing God. He concludes that there are many such reports. The Mu'tazila denial is thus presented as a rejection of clear revealed texts.

Key Terms
رؤية الله (ru'yat Allāh)
المعاد (al-ma'ād)
ناظرة (nāẓira)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Mu'tazila affirmed a metaphorical vision of God.
Correction: The Mu'tazila explicitly denied any vision of God, even in the afterlife, as stated in the passage.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani refute the Mu'tazila denial of seeing God?
A) By logical arguments
B) By citing Qur'an and hadith
C) By consensus
D) By appealing to reason

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila denial of seeing God is refuted by explicit Quranic verses and prophetic hadith, affirming that believers will see their Lord in the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said you will see your Lord as clearly as the full moon. Does that truth fill you with hope and longing, or have you become numb to it? What is one concrete change in your daily routine that will remind you of this coming encounter?
?
Where in your life have you followed your own reasoning over clear divine texts, just as the Mu'tazila did? Identify one decision or belief where you need to surrender your intellect to revelation, and commit to doing so today.
?
If you truly believed that in the Hereafter you will see God face to face, how would that change the way you spend this evening? Write down one action you will take before bed to prepare for that vision.

Establishing the Principle: Allah's Face is an Attribute, Not a Limb
Baqillani presents the proof from the Quran that Allah's face is His essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Quranic verse 'And there remains the Face of your Lord' establishes that Allah's face is His essence, not a physical limb, refuting anthropomorphism.

Core Idea
Allah's face is His essence, not a limb.

In this lesson, we begin with the foundational question: How do we know that Allah has a face and hands? Imam Baqillani answers by first distinguishing true reports from physical interpretations. We will examine the Quranic evidence that 'face' means the essence of Allah, as understood by early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening objection and answer
Notice how the question requests proof for Allah having a face and hands, and the immediate response that it is from a true report describing a quality, not a form.
The Arabic term 'al-khabar al-sadiq' refers to the Quran and authentic hadith.
2
Analyze the Quranic verse and its interpretation
Focus on the verse 'And there remains the Face of your Lord' and the interpretations by Ibn al-Jawzi, al-Dahhak, and Abu Ubayda that 'face' means the essence.
'Everything is perishing except His Face' is taken as proof that 'Face' means 'He' (the Essence).
3
Understand the refutation of anthropomorphism
See how this verse is used to invalidate the belief that Allah has physical limbs, establishing the correct understanding of the attribute.
The passage explicitly rejects claims of a 'particular limb'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبواب شتى في الصفات باب في أن الله وجهاً ويدين. فإن قال قائل: فما الحجّة في أن الله عزّ وجلّ وجهاً ويدين؟ اعلم أنه ثبت في الخبر الصادق وبه قال الله تعالى صفة لا من حيث الصورة. أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: (ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام). قال ابن الجوزي في دفع الشبه: قال المفسرون وينفي ربك وكذا قالوا في قوله تعالى يريدون وجهه أي يريدونه. وقال الضحاك وأبو عبيدة: كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه أي إلا هو. وهذا هو الحق الذي قام البرهان بصحته لبطلان القول بالتجسيم. وقال تعالى أيضاً كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه. وهذه الآية نص على أن المراد بالوجه الذات لا صفة من الصفات ولا عضو من الأعضاء، فالقول بأنه صفة غير وجيه، أمام هذه الآية التي تفسر المراد بالوجه، بحيث لا تدع وجهاً للتقول كائناً من كان المتقول: خلفياً كان أو سلفياً، وأما جملة على العضو المخصوص كما هو مذهب المجسمة فمردوداً أيضاً بهذه الآية وقد تضافرت الأدلة على أن من يتوهم في معبوده الأعضاء فهو على الوثنية الأولى وإن تظاهر بالاهتداء. وأما الأخبار فكثيرة منها ما رواه مسلم والبخاري وغيرهم. قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «جنتان من فضة آنيتهما وما فيهما، وجنتان من ذهب آنيتهما وما فيهما، وما بين القوم وبين أن ينظروا إلى ربهم عزّ وجلّ إلا رداء الكبرياء على وجهه في جنة عدن». وقوله: «رداء الكبرياء» يريد به صفة الكبرياء فهو بكبريائه وعظمته لا يريد أن يراه أحد من خلقه بعد رؤية يوم القيامة حتى يأذن لهم بدخول جنة عدن، فإذا دخلوها أراد أن يروه فيروه وهم في جنة عدن وهو ليس في الجنة تعالى الله أن يحويه مكان. وروي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما فيما يرويه البيهقي أنه رأى رجلا يصلي يلتفت في صلاته فقال ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: إن الله عزّ وجلّ مقبل إلى عبده بوجهه ما أقبل إليه فإذا التفت انصرف عنه. واعلم أنه ليس في صفات ذات الله عزّ وجلّ إقبال ولا إعراض ولا صرف وإنما ذلك في صفات فعله وكأن الرحمة التي للوجه تعلق بها تعلق الصفة بمقتضاها تأتيه من قبل وجه المصلي، فعبر به عن إقبال تلك الرحمة وصرفها وإقبال الوجه وصرفه لتعلق الوجه الذي هو صفة بها والله أعلم. والذي يبين صحة هذا التأويل ما روي عن أبي ذر رضي الله عنه يبلغ به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إذا قام أحدكم إلى الصلاة فإن الرحمة تواجهه فلا يمس الحصا». وشائع في كلام الناس: الأمير مقبل على فلان، وهم يريدون به إقباله عليه بالإحسان ومعرض عن فلان وهم يريدون به ترك إحسانه إليه وصرف إنعامه عنه والله أعلم. والآثار في معنى هذا عن النبي وأصحابه وأتباعهم رضي الله عنهم أجمعين كثيرة.
Various chapters on the attributes. Chapter on that Allah has a face and two hands. If a questioner says: What is the proof that Allah, may He be glorified and exalted, has a face and two hands? Know that it is established in the true report, and by it Allah said a description not in terms of form. As for the Book, His saying: 'And there remains the Face of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor.' Ibn al-Jawzi said in 'Deflecting the Doubt': The commentators said 'and your Lord remains' and likewise they said regarding His saying 'they desire His face' meaning they desire Him. And al-Dahhak and Abu Ubayda said: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' meaning except Him. This is the truth, the proof of which has been established, invalidating the statement of anthropomorphism. And He also said: 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' This verse is textual evidence that what is meant by 'face' is the essence, not an attribute nor a limb. Therefore, saying it is an attribute is not sound, before this verse which interprets the meaning of 'face', such that it leaves no room for speculation from anyone, whether he be a Khalafi or a Salafi. As for the statement about the particular limb, as is the doctrine of the anthropomorphists, it is also rejected by this verse. And the proofs have accumulated that whoever imagines limbs for his deity is upon the first idolatry, even if he outwardly claims guidance. As for the reports, they are many, including what Muslim, al-Bukhari and others narrated. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Two gardens of silver, their vessels and what is in them, and two gardens of gold, their vessels and what is in them. And nothing prevents the people from looking at their Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, except the cloak of pride upon His face in the Garden of Eden.' His saying 'cloak of pride' means the attribute of pride. So He, through His pride and majesty, does not want any of His creation to see Him after the vision on the Day of Resurrection until He permits them to enter the Garden of Eden. When they enter it, He wants them to see Him, so they see Him while they are in the Garden of Eden, and He is not in the Garden—exalted is Allah from being contained by a place. And it is narrated from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, in what al-Bayhaqi narrates, that he saw a man praying while looking around in his prayer. Ibn Umar said: 'Indeed Allah, may He be glorified and exalted, turns towards His servant with His face as long as he turns towards Him. When he turns away, He turns away from him.' And know that there is no turning towards, turning away, or turning aside in the attributes of Allah's essence; rather that is in His attributes of action. And it is as though mercy that belongs to the face is attached to it with the attachment of an attribute by its requirement, coming to him from the direction of the worshipper's face. So by it is expressed the turning towards of that mercy and its turning away, and the turning towards of the face and its turning away, because of the attachment of the face, which is an attribute, to it. And Allah knows best. What shows the correctness of this interpretation is what is narrated from Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, raising it to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'When one of you stands for prayer, mercy faces him, so he should not touch pebbles.' And it is common in people's speech: 'The prince is turning towards so-and-so,' meaning he is turning to him with beneficence, and 'turning away from so-and-so,' meaning he is abandoning his beneficence to him and turning away his favor from him. And Allah knows best. The reports about the meaning of this from the Prophet, his Companions, and their followers, may Allah be pleased with them all, are many.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a structured objection-and-answer argument. It begins with a chapter heading affirming that Allah has a face and two hands. Then an objector asks for the proof. The answer is given in parts: First, it establishes that these are attributes declared in true reports, not physical forms. Then it presents Quranic evidence, specifically the verse 'And there remains the Face of your Lord...', citing interpretations from early scholars (Ibn al-Jawzi, al-Dahhak, Abu Ubayda) that 'face' here means the essence of Allah, not a limb. It argues that this verse refutes anthropomorphism. Then it presents Hadith evidence, including the famous hadith about the two gardens and the 'cloak of pride' on Allah's face, explaining that this does not imply a physical face but an attribute. It also narrates a tradition from Ibn Umar about Allah turning to a worshipper with His face, clarifying that this is an attribute of action, not of essence. Finally, it supports this interpretation with the hadith of Abu Dharr about mercy facing the worshipper, and uses common Arabic speech as an analogy. The conclusion is that these attributes are real but not anthropomorphic.

Key Terms
وجه
الخبر الصادق
تجسيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Affirming that Allah has a face means He has a physical face like humans.
Correction: The Quranic verse and classical exegesis show that 'face' here means the essence of Allah, not a limb.

Checkpoint
What is the main Quranic evidence used to prove that 'face' refers to Allah's essence and not a limb?
And there remains the Face of your Lord
To Allah belongs the East and the West
He is the First and the Last
And He is with you wherever you are

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse 'And there remains the Face of your Lord' is the primary evidence that Allah's face is His essence, not a limb.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read verses like 'the Face of your Lord', do you instinctively imagine a face like a human's? What does that reveal about your mind's tendency to compare Allah to creation, and how will you fight that tendency after this lesson?
?
This lesson shows that early scholars interpreted 'face' as essence. Have you ever accepted a popular or literal interpretation of an attribute without checking the understanding of the salaf? Will you commit to seeking their tafsir before forming beliefs about Allah?
?
If someone accuses you of believing in a physical face for Allah, can you now defend the correct belief using the very verse they misuse? What would you say to them from this passage to clarify the truth?

Hadith Evidence: The Face of Allah in the Two Gardens Hadith and the Turning of the Face
Baqillani provides hadith evidence for the attribute of face.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith about the two gardens and the cloak of pride, and the tradition from Ibn Umar about Allah turning to the worshipper, affirm the attribute of face without implying a physical body.

Core Idea
The Prophet's descriptions of Allah's face in hadith are attributes of majesty, not physical limbs.

After the Quranic evidence, Imam Baqillani presents prophetic hadith that mention Allah's face. The famous 'two gardens' hadith speaks of the 'cloak of pride upon His face', and Ibn Umar's tradition describes Allah turning towards the worshipper. We will see how these are interpreted to mean attributes of action and majesty, not physicality.

Guided Path
1
Read the two gardens hadith and its explanation
Pay attention to the phrase 'cloak of pride upon His face' and Baqillani's interpretation that this refers to the attribute of pride.
The hadith indicates that Allah will be seen in the Garden of Eden, but He is not contained in any place.
2
Study the Ibn Umar tradition about turning of the face
Note that Ibn Umar says Allah turns to His worshipper with His face as long as the worshipper faces Him, and turns away when the worshipper turns away.
This is an attribute of action, not essence.
3
Distinguish between attributes of essence and action
Baqillani explicitly states that turning and turning away are not in the attributes of essence but in attributes of action, related to mercy.
The 'face' itself is an attribute of essence, but its turning is an action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray, do you truly believe that Allah, in His majesty, turns His face towards you as long as you face Him? Or does your mind wander, turning away from His mercy? Today, commit to praying with the awareness that His face is oriented towards you.
?
The hadith says nothing prevents the people from looking at their Lord except the cloak of pride upon His face. This pride is an attribute of majesty. How does knowing that Allah's pride veils Him affect your awe of Him? Do you live with that reverence?
?
Baqillani emphasizes that Allah is not contained by any place, not even Jannah. Does your heart ever imagine Allah as being 'somewhere'? Repent from that imagination and affirm His transcendence, training your heart to worship Him without spatial boundaries.

Reconciling Attributes: The Face of Allah as an Attribute of Essence and the Analogical Interpretation
Baqillani uses an analogy from common speech to explain the attribute of face.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the analogy of common speech ('the prince is turning towards so-and-so') helps explain that Allah's face is an attribute, not a limb, and that the correct interpretation avoids anthropomorphism while affirming the attribute.

Core Idea
The face of Allah is a real attribute, understood through the language of honor and mercy, not physicality.

After presenting the proof, Imam Baqillani further clarifies the interpretation by using an analogy from everyday Arabic speech. When we say 'the prince turned towards so-and-so,' we mean he showed kindness, not that he physically turned. Similarly, Allah's face and its turning are understood as expressions of mercy. This final lesson ties together the earlier evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith of Abu Dharr about mercy facing the worshipper
Notice that the Prophet says 'mercy faces him' – this supports the interpretation that 'facing' is about mercy, not physical direction.
The hadith encourages focus in prayer, as mercy is directed towards the worshipper.
2
Analyze the analogy from common speech
Consider how 'the prince is turning towards so-and-so' means he is showing beneficence, not physically turning. This analogy clarifies the meaning of Allah's attributes.
Baqillani uses this to show that language allows for non-physical attribution.
3
Reflect on the overall conclusion
Understand that the attributes of face and hands are real but free from anthropomorphism, as supported by all the evidence.
The reports from the Prophet and companions on this topic are abundant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أبواب شتى في الصفات باب في أن الله وجهاً ويدين. فإن قال قائل: فما الحجّة في أن الله عزّ وجلّ وجهاً ويدين؟ اعلم أنه ثبت في الخبر الصادق وبه قال الله تعالى صفة لا من حيث الصورة. أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: (ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام). قال ابن الجوزي في دفع الشبه: قال المفسرون وينفي ربك وكذا قالوا في قوله تعالى يريدون وجهه أي يريدونه. وقال الضحاك وأبو عبيدة: كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه أي إلا هو. وهذا هو الحق الذي قام البرهان بصحته لبطلان القول بالتجسيم. وقال تعالى أيضاً كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه. وهذه الآية نص على أن المراد بالوجه الذات لا صفة من الصفات ولا عضو من الأعضاء، فالقول بأنه صفة غير وجيه، أمام هذه الآية التي تفسر المراد بالوجه، بحيث لا تدع وجهاً للتقول كائناً من كان المتقول: خلفياً كان أو سلفياً، وأما جملة على العضو المخصوص كما هو مذهب المجسمة فمردوداً أيضاً بهذه الآية وقد تضافرت الأدلة على أن من يتوهم في معبوده الأعضاء فهو على الوثنية الأولى وإن تظاهر بالاهتداء. وأما الأخبار فكثيرة منها ما رواه مسلم والبخاري وغيرهم. قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «جنتان من فضة آنيتهما وما فيهما، وجنتان من ذهب آنيتهما وما فيهما، وما بين القوم وبين أن ينظروا إلى ربهم عزّ وجلّ إلا رداء الكبرياء على وجهه في جنة عدن». وقوله: «رداء الكبرياء» يريد به صفة الكبرياء فهو بكبريائه وعظمته لا يريد أن يراه أحد من خلقه بعد رؤية يوم القيامة حتى يأذن لهم بدخول جنة عدن، فإذا دخلوها أراد أن يروه فيروه وهم في جنة عدن وهو ليس في الجنة تعالى الله أن يحويه مكان. وروي عن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما فيما يرويه البيهقي أنه رأى رجلا يصلي يلتفت في صلاته فقال ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما: إن الله عزّ وجلّ مقبل إلى عبده بوجهه ما أقبل إليه فإذا التفت انصرف عنه. واعلم أنه ليس في صفات ذات الله عزّ وجلّ إقبال ولا إعراض ولا صرف وإنما ذلك في صفات فعله وكأن الرحمة التي للوجه تعلق بها تعلق الصفة بمقتضاها تأتيه من قبل وجه المصلي، فعبر به عن إقبال تلك الرحمة وصرفها وإقبال الوجه وصرفه لتعلق الوجه الذي هو صفة بها والله أعلم. والذي يبين صحة هذا التأويل ما روي عن أبي ذر رضي الله عنه يبلغ به النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إذا قام أحدكم إلى الصلاة فإن الرحمة تواجهه فلا يمس الحصا». وشائع في كلام الناس: الأمير مقبل على فلان، وهم يريدون به إقباله عليه بالإحسان ومعرض عن فلان وهم يريدون به ترك إحسانه إليه وصرف إنعامه عنه والله أعلم. والآثار في معنى هذا عن النبي وأصحابه وأتباعهم رضي الله عنهم أجمعين كثيرة.
Various chapters on the attributes. Chapter on that Allah has a face and two hands. If a questioner says: What is the proof that Allah, may He be glorified and exalted, has a face and two hands? Know that it is established in the true report, and by it Allah said a description not in terms of form. As for the Book, His saying: 'And there remains the Face of your Lord, Possessor of Majesty and Honor.' Ibn al-Jawzi said in 'Deflecting the Doubt': The commentators said 'and your Lord remains' and likewise they said regarding His saying 'they desire His face' meaning they desire Him. And al-Dahhak and Abu Ubayda said: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' meaning except Him. This is the truth, the proof of which has been established, invalidating the statement of anthropomorphism. And He also said: 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' This verse is textual evidence that what is meant by 'face' is the essence, not an attribute nor a limb. Therefore, saying it is an attribute is not sound, before this verse which interprets the meaning of 'face', such that it leaves no room for speculation from anyone, whether he be a Khalafi or a Salafi. As for the statement about the particular limb, as is the doctrine of the anthropomorphists, it is also rejected by this verse. And the proofs have accumulated that whoever imagines limbs for his deity is upon the first idolatry, even if he outwardly claims guidance. As for the reports, they are many, including what Muslim, al-Bukhari and others narrated. The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Two gardens of silver, their vessels and what is in them, and two gardens of gold, their vessels and what is in them. And nothing prevents the people from looking at their Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, except the cloak of pride upon His face in the Garden of Eden.' His saying 'cloak of pride' means the attribute of pride. So He, through His pride and majesty, does not want any of His creation to see Him after the vision on the Day of Resurrection until He permits them to enter the Garden of Eden. When they enter it, He wants them to see Him, so they see Him while they are in the Garden of Eden, and He is not in the Garden—exalted is Allah from being contained by a place. And it is narrated from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, in what al-Bayhaqi narrates, that he saw a man praying while looking around in his prayer. Ibn Umar said: 'Indeed Allah, may He be glorified and exalted, turns towards His servant with His face as long as he turns towards Him. When he turns away, He turns away from him.' And know that there is no turning towards, turning away, or turning aside in the attributes of Allah's essence; rather that is in His attributes of action. And it is as though mercy that belongs to the face is attached to it with the attachment of an attribute by its requirement, coming to him from the direction of the worshipper's face. So by it is expressed the turning towards of that mercy and its turning away, and the turning towards of the face and its turning away, because of the attachment of the face, which is an attribute, to it. And Allah knows best. What shows the correctness of this interpretation is what is narrated from Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him, raising it to the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, who said: 'When one of you stands for prayer, mercy faces him, so he should not touch pebbles.' And it is common in people's speech: 'The prince is turning towards so-and-so,' meaning he is turning to him with beneficence, and 'turning away from so-and-so,' meaning he is abandoning his beneficence to him and turning away his favor from him. And Allah knows best. The reports about the meaning of this from the Prophet, his Companions, and their followers, may Allah be pleased with them all, are many.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a structured objection-and-answer argument. It begins with a chapter heading affirming that Allah has a face and two hands. Then an objector asks for the proof. The answer is given in parts: First, it establishes that these are attributes declared in true reports, not physical forms. Then it presents Quranic evidence, specifically the verse 'And there remains the Face of your Lord...', citing interpretations from early scholars (Ibn al-Jawzi, al-Dahhak, Abu Ubayda) that 'face' here means the essence of Allah, not a limb. It argues that this verse refutes anthropomorphism. Then it presents Hadith evidence, including the famous hadith about the two gardens and the 'cloak of pride' on Allah's face, explaining that this does not imply a physical face but an attribute. It also narrates a tradition from Ibn Umar about Allah turning to a worshipper with His face, clarifying that this is an attribute of action, not of essence. Finally, it supports this interpretation with the hadith of Abu Dharr about mercy facing the worshipper, and uses common Arabic speech as an analogy. The conclusion is that these attributes are real but not anthropomorphic.

تأويل
رحمة
إقبال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The analogical interpretation implies that the attributes are not real or are purely metaphorical without reality.
Correction: The attributes are real, but their modality is understood through language that befits Allah; they are not mere metaphors.

Checkpoint

That turning towards means showing beneficence, not physical movement
That the prince has a face like a human

Key Takeaway
The analogy of common speech shows that describing Allah's face as turning towards a worshipper means His mercy is directed to him, without any physical movement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If a prince turned to you with his favor, you would feel immense gratitude and behave with utmost respect. Do you approach Allah as if He has turned His face toward you in mercy? What, if anything, holds you back from that awareness?
?
The analogy shows that language about Allah must be understood through the lens of what is befitting to Him. Are there any attributes of Allah that you have unintentionally imagined in human terms? Commit today to study them with the understanding that they are real but beyond your comprehension, and let that awe transform your worship.

Proof for Allah's Face and Hands from Quran
Baqillani states the proof for affirming face and hands from Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses explicit Quranic verses to affirm the attributes of face and hands for Allah.

Core Idea
Allah's face and hands are proven by clear Quranic texts, not by metaphor.

In this short passage, Baqillani presents the foundational proof for two divine attributes: face (wajh) and hands (yadayn). He uses a question-and-answer format to show that these attributes are directly mentioned in the Quran. This lesson examines the verses and the logic behind their use as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the concise style and the use of Quranic verses as proof.
The passage begins with a chapter heading that states the doctrine.
2
Identify the objector's question
The objector asks: 'What is the proof that Allah has a face and two hands?' This sets up the need for evidence.
This format shows that the doctrine is not assumed but must be supported.
3
Analyze the two Quranic verses
The first verse (55:27) mentions 'face' directly. The second (38:75) mentions 'two hands'. Both are cited as textual proof.
These are clear, explicit texts (nass) according to Baqillani.
4
Understand the conclusion
The responder concludes that Allah affirmed for Himself a face and two hands. This is the direct implication of the verses.
No metaphorical interpretation is offered; the texts are taken literally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في أن الله وجهاً ويدين
فإن قال قائل : فما الحجّة في أن الله عزّ وجلّ وجهاً ويدين؟
قيل له: قوله تعالى: ﴿ويبقى وجه ربك ذو الجلال والإكرام﴾، وقوله: ﴿ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي﴾. فأثبت لنفسه وجهاً ويدين.
Chapter: That Allah has a face and two hands. For if someone says: What is the proof that Allah Almighty has a face and two hands? It is said to him: His saying, the Most High: 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord, Owner of Majesty and Honor' (55:27), and His saying: 'What prevented you from prostrating to that which I created with My two hands?' (38:75). So He affirmed for Himself a face and two hands.

Commentary
This passage is a definition-and-proof unit. It begins with a chapter heading stating the doctrine that Allah has a face (wajh) and two hands (yadayn). Then an objector asks for the proof. The answer cites two Quranic verses: first, 'And there will remain the Face of your Lord' (55:27), which directly mentions 'face'; second, 'What prevented you from prostrating to that which I created with My two hands?' (38:75), which directly mentions 'two hands'. The conclusion is that these verses establish the attributes of face and hands for Allah. The argument is straightforward: the objector demands evidence, and the responder provides explicit Quranic texts.

Correction: Baqillani takes these verses at face value as literal proof of the attributes. He does not engage in allegorical interpretation here, asserting that the texts clearly affirm face and hands.

Refuting Metaphorical Interpretations of 'Hand' in the Quran
Baqillani refutes the metaphorical interpretation of 'yad' as power or favor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani rejects metaphorical readings of 'yad' (hand) in the verse about Adam's creation and how he establishes that it must refer to actual divine attributes.

Core Idea
Metaphor for 'hand' undermines Adam's honor; only actual attributes preserve it.

In this passage, Baqillani responds to those who claim that 'yad' in the Quranic verse 'I created with My two hands' means power or favor. He systematically shows why such interpretations fail, using linguistic and theological reasoning. Read on to see how he defends the literal attribution of 'hand' as a divine attribute without falling into anthropomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Learn what the objectors claim: that 'yad' can mean power or favor based on linguistic usage.
The objectors are trying to avoid anthropomorphism by interpreting 'hand' metaphorically.
2
Follow Baqillani's rejection
See why he rejects each possible interpretation, especially the one that would make Iblis share in Adam's honor.
Baqillani argues that interpreting 'yad' as power or favor would imply that both Adam and Iblis share that attribute, nullifying Adam's special status.
3
Grasp the conclusion
Understand that 'yad' here indicates two specific attributes, preserving the special status of Adam.
Baqillani establishes a general principle: whenever 'yad' is mentioned with specification, it indicates an attribute specially attached to the thing mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا فما أنكرتم أن يكون المعنى في قوله: ﴿خلقت بيدي﴾ أنه خلقه بقدرته أو بنعمته؟ لأن اليد في اللغة قد تكون بمعنى القوة والمالك والنعمة والصلة والجارحة. فأما قوله عزّ وجلّ: ﴿يا إبليس ما منعك أن تسجد لما خلقت بيدي﴾ فلا يجوز أن يحمل على الجارحة، لأن الباري جلّ جلاله واحد ولا يجوز عليه التبعيض، ولا القوة والملك والنعمة والصلة لأن الاشتراك يقع حينئذ بين ولي آدم وعدوه إبليس فيبطل ما ذكر من تفضيله عليه لبطلان معنى التخصيص، فلم يبق إلا أن يحملا على صفتين تعلقتا بخلق آدم تشريفاً له دون خلق إبليس وذلك بالحمل على معنى العناية الخاصة. وكذلك كل موضع جرى ذكرها على طريق التخصيص فإنه يقتضى تعلق الصفة التي تسمى بالسمع يداً بالكائن فيما خص بذكر ما فيه تعلق الصفة بمقتضاها، ثم لا يكون في ذلك بطلان موضع تفضيل آدم عليه السلام على إبليس لأن التخصيص إذا وجد له في معنى دون إبليس لم يضر مشاركة غيره إياه في ذلك المعنى، بعد أن لم يشاركه فيه إبليس والله أعلم.
For if they say: Why do you not accept that the meaning in His saying: 'I created with My two hands' is that He created him by His power or His favor? Because 'hand' in the language can mean power, ownership, favor, connection, and the limb. As for His saying, the Most High: 'O Iblis, what prevented you from prostrating to that which I created with My two hands?' It is not permissible to interpret it as the limb, because the Creator, exalted is His majesty, is One, and division is not permissible for Him. Nor [can it be interpreted as] power, ownership, favor, or connection, because then partnership (al-ish̲tirāk) would occur between the friend of Adam and his enemy Iblis, thus nullifying the mentioned preference of him due to the nullification of the meaning of specification (al-takhṣīṣ). So nothing remains except that they be interpreted as two attributes that are attached to the creation of Adam as an honor for him, not for the creation of Iblis, and that by interpreting them as meaning special care. And likewise, every place where they are mentioned in the way of specification, it requires the attachment of the attribute that is called 'hand' by revelation to the thing specifically mentioned, in which the attribute's implication is attached. Then there is no nullification of the place of preference of Adam over Iblis, because if specification is found for him in a meaning not shared by Iblis, it does not harm that someone else shares with him in that meaning, after that Iblis does not share it with him. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The objectors propose that 'hand' in the verse could metaphorically mean power (qudra) or favor (ni‘ma), based on linguistic usage. Baqillani responds by first listing the possible meanings of 'yad' in Arabic: power, ownership, favor, connection (sila), and the literal limb. Then he argues that for the specific verse about Adam, none of these common interpretations work. Interpreting 'yad' as a limb is impossible because Allah is not a body. Interpreting it as power or favor would imply that both Adam and Iblis share in that attribute, thereby undermining the special honor of Adam over Iblis. So the only remaining possibility is that 'yad' here refers to two actual divine attributes (ṣifāt) that are specifically attached to the creation of Adam as an honor. This preserves the distinction between Adam and Iblis. Baqillani concludes with a general principle: whenever 'yad' is mentioned with specification (takhṣīṣ), it indicates an attribute specially attached to the thing mentioned. Thus, the attribute of 'hand' is established without compromising tawhid or the specificity of honor.

يد
قدرة
نعمة
اشتراك
تخصيص
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'yad' in the verse 'I created with My two hands' must be interpreted metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism.
Correction: Baqillani shows that metaphorical interpretations like power or favor lead to theological contradictions (undermining Adam's honor), so 'yad' must refer to actual divine attributes.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject interpreting 'yad' as power or favor in the verse about Adam?
A) Because power and favor are not divine attributes
B) Because then both Adam and Iblis would share the same attribute, nullifying Adam's special honor
C) Because the verse explicitly says 'yad' means limb
D) Because power and favor cannot be attributed to Allah

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the only consistent interpretation of 'yad' in the Adam verse is as two actual divine attributes, not metaphors for power or favor.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'I created with My two hands,' does it move you to feel that you are specially created by Allah with His own hands (through Adam)? Does that thought change how you live today, or do you treat it as just an old story?
?
Baqillani warns that reducing Allah's hand to a metaphor of 'power' strips Adam of his unique honor. In your own life, do you ever reduce Allah's personal attributes—like His mercy or anger—to impersonal forces to avoid feeling personally accountable?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's 'hand' is a real attribute that specially honored Adam, how would that affect your understanding of your own worth and purpose? Are you living as if you were created with special care, or do you act as if you were simply another creature like Iblis?

Refutation of Interpreting 'Hand' as Power or Blessing
Baqillani refutes the interpretation of yad as power or blessing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Baqillani argues that interpreting Allah's 'hands' as power or blessing is false and why the literal meaning must be affirmed.

Core Idea
The two hands of Allah cannot be reduced to power or blessing without contradiction.

Imam Baqillani addresses a common metaphorical interpretation of the Qur'anic phrase 'My hands' in the verse about Adam's creation. Some scholars claimed 'yad' means power or blessing. Baqillani refutes this by showing it leads to absurdities and contradicts Muslim consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to how Baqillani presents the opponents' evidence before refuting it.
2
Identify the opponents' evidence
The passage begins by presenting arguments that 'yad' can mean power or blessing. Find the linguistic examples and Qur'anic citation they use.
These include expressions like 'white hand' for blessing and 'under his hand' for power.
3
Follow Baqillani's refutation
Baqillani gives three arguments: (1) two hands would mean two powers, contradicting consensus; (2) two hands as two blessings is absurd because blessings are countless; (3) linguistic usage does not allow 'hand' to mean blessing in the relevant contexts.
Consider why each argument invalidates the metaphorical interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بمعنى النعمة وبمعنى القدرة، كما يقال: «لي عند فلان يد بيضاء» يراد به نعمة؛ وكما يقال: هذا الشيء في يد فلان وتحت يد فلان يراد به أنه تحت قدرته وفي ملكه. ويقال: رجل أيد إذا كان قادراً. وكما قال الله تعالى: خلقنا لهم مما عملت أيدينا أنعاماً يريد عملنا بقدرتنا. قال الشاعر: إذا ما راية رفعت لمجد تلقاها عرابة باليمين. فكذلك قوله: خلقت بيدي يعني: بقدرتي أو نعمتي. يقال لهم: هذا باطل، لأن قوله بيدي يقتضي إثبات يدين هما صفة له. فلو كان المراد بهما القدرة لوجب أن يكون له قدرتان. وأنتم فلا تزعمون أن للباري سبحانه قدرة واحدة فكيف يجوز أن تثبتوا له قدرتين؟ وقد أجمع المسلمون من مثبتي الصفات والنافين لها، على أنه لا يجوز أن يكون له تعالى قدرتان فبطل ما قلتم. وكذلك لا يجوز أن يكون الله تعالى خلق آدم بنعمتين، لأن نعم الله تعالى على آدم وعلى غيره لا تحصى. ولأن القائل لا يجوز أن يقول «رفعت الشيء بيدي»، أو وضعته بيدي، أو توليته بيدي وهو يعني نعمته. وكذلك لا يجوز أن يقال لي عند فلان يدان يعني نعمتين وإنما يقال لي عنده يدان بيضاوان. لأن القول «يد» لا يستعمل إلا في اليد التي هي صفة للذات.
With the meaning of blessing and with the meaning of power, as is said: 'I have a white hand with so-and-so' meaning a blessing; and as is said: 'This thing is in the hand of so-and-so and under the hand of so-and-so' meaning that it is under his power and in his possession. And it is said: 'a man ayyad' if he is powerful. And as Allah Most High said: 'We created for them from what Our hands worked cattle' meaning 'We worked with Our power.' The poet said: 'When a banner is raised for glory, 'Uraba receives it with the right hand.' So likewise His saying 'I created with My hands' means 'with My power' or 'My blessing.' It is said to them: This is false, because His saying 'with My hands' necessitates affirming two hands that are an attribute of Him. If the intended meaning were power, then He would have to have two powers. And you (opponents) do not claim that the Creator (subhanahu) has one power (only), so how can it be permissible for you to affirm two powers for Him? And the Muslims, both those who affirm attributes and those who negate them, have agreed that it is not permissible for Him (ta'ala) to have two powers, so what you said is invalid. And likewise it is not permissible that Allah (ta'ala) created Adam with two blessings, because the blessings of Allah (ta'ala) upon Adam and others are countless. And because the speaker cannot say 'I raised the thing with my hand' or 'I put it down with my hand' or 'I undertook it with my hand' meaning His blessing. And likewise it is not permissible to say 'I have two hands with so-and-so' meaning two blessings; rather it is said 'I have two white hands with him.' Because the word 'hand' is not used except for the hand that is an attribute of the Essence.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the metaphorical interpretation of the word 'yad' (hand) when attributed to Allah in the Qur'an, specifically the verse 'I created with My hands.' The opponents claim that 'yad' here means power or blessing, not a literal hand. Baqillani first presents their evidence: the word 'yad' can mean blessing in expressions like 'I have a white hand with so-and-so' (i.e., a favor), and it can mean power when saying 'it is in his hand' or describing a man as 'ayyad' (powerful). They also cite the Qur'anic verse 'Our hands worked' interpreted as 'Our power,' and a poetic line about receiving a banner 'with the right hand' as a metaphor for power. However, Baqillani then argues that this interpretation is false. First, the phrase 'with My hands' in the verse about Adam's creation explicitly mentions two hands. If these two hands were simply power, then Allah would have two powers. But the opponents themselves, including Mu'tazilites who negate attributes, agree that Allah has only one power (since they affirm one attribute of power). This consensus proves that the interpretation leads to an impossibility. Second, if 'hands' meant blessing, then creating Adam with two blessings would be absurd because Allah's blessings are innumerable, not limited to two. Moreover, in common language, if one says 'I raised something with my hand,' it cannot be understood to mean 'with my blessing.' The word 'hand' in such contexts always refers to the literal hand. When a favor is intended, the phrase is 'I have two white hands with him,' not simply 'two hands.' Thus, the only consistent meaning is that 'yad' is a real attribute of Allah, not a metaphorical expression.

Key Terms
يد (yad)
قدرة (power)
نعمة (blessing)
صفة (attribute)
إثبات الصفات (affirmation of attributes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'yad' in the Qur'an can be safely interpreted as power or blessing without theological consequences.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this interpretation leads to contradictions: it would imply two powers (contradicting consensus) or two blessings (absurd), and it conflicts with linguistic usage.

Checkpoint
What is the main problem with interpreting 'yad' in 'خلقت بيدي' as power (قدرة)?
A) It implies Allah has a physical hand.
B) It would require Allah to have two powers, which contradicts Muslim consensus.
C) The word 'yad' never means power in Arabic.
D) Allah's power is unknowable.

Key Takeaway
Interpreting Allah's attribute of 'hand' as power or blessing contradicts Muslim consensus and linguistic usage, thus the literal affirmation of the attribute is necessary.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'yad Allah' are you satisfied with a mere metaphor that keeps you at a safe distance, or do you truly believe that Allah has hands that are real yet beyond your imagination? How does your answer shape the awe you feel when you pray?
?
If you are honest, do you ever explain away Allah's attributes to avoid the weight of His transcendence? What would it mean for your daily life to affirm that Allah's hand is a real and perfect attribute—and that He created Adam with His own hands?
?
The opponents used language to avoid anthropomorphism, but Baqillani exposed that as a contradiction. Are there areas in your faith where you prefer comfortable interpretations over what the Qur'an and Sunnah literally require? What will you do about that today?

The Iblis Evidence and the Objection on Divine Body Parts
Baqillani adds the Iblis proof and answers the objection about body parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes metaphorical interpretations of divine attributes through the Iblis argument and how he defends the possibility of non-corporeal attributes.

Core Idea
If 'hand' meant power, Iblis would have used that to avoid prostrating, but he didn't – proving it's a real attribute.

Imam al-Baqillani continues his refutation of those who interpret 'hand' and 'face' as mere metaphors. He presents a powerful argument from the Quranic story of Iblis, showing that even the devil understood 'hand' as a special honor. Then he addresses a common objection: how can we affirm these attributes without making Allah physical? His answer draws on the broader principle that Allah's attributes are not bound by our limited experience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage divides into two clear parts: the Iblis evidence and the objection-answer.
2
Understand the Iblis evidence
Baqillani argues that if 'yad' meant power or blessing, Iblis would have argued that he too was created by that power, so why should he prostrate? The fact that Iblis did not use this argument shows he knew the literal meaning was a special honor.
3
Examine the objection and answer
The objector says: we cannot conceive of a hand or face that is not a body part, so how can you affirm them for Allah? Baqillani responds by pointing to other attributes we affirm despite lacking examples in the created world.
Pay attention to the two analogies: living/knowing/powerful without a body, and self-subsistent without being a substance.
4
Reflect on the principle
The key principle is that we do not limit Allah to what we experience. Just as we affirm that Allah knows without a brain, we can affirm He has a hand without a limb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدل على فساد تأويلهم أيضاً أنه لو كان الأمر على ما قالوه، لم يغفل عن ذلك إبليس وعن أن يقول: وأي فضل لآدم علي يقتضي أن أسجد له، وأنا أيضاً بيدك خلقتني، التي هي قدرتك، وبنعمتك خلقتني؟ وفي العلم بأن الله تعالى فضل آدم عليه بخلقه بيديه دليل على فساد ما قالوه. فإن قال قائل: فما تنكرون أن يكون وجهه ويده جارحة، إذ كنتم لم تعقلوا يد صفة ووجه صفة لا جارحة؟ يقال له: لا يجب ذلك، كما لا يجب، إذا لم نعقل حياً عالماً قادراً إلا جسماً، أن نقضي نحن وأنتم على الله تعالى بذلك. وكما لا يجب، متى كان قائماً بذاته، أن يكون جوهراً أو جسماً، لأنا وإياكم لم نجد قائماً بنفسه في شاهدنا إلا كذلك.
And it also indicates the corruption of their interpretation that if the matter were as they said, Iblis would not have been heedless of that and would not have said: 'And what virtue does Adam have over me that obliges me to prostrate to him, while I also was created by Your hand, which is Your power, and by Your blessing You created me?' And in the knowledge that Allah (ta'ala) favored Adam over him by creating him with His two hands is evidence of the corruption of what they said. If a questioner says: 'Then why do you deny that His face and hand are a body part (jarha), since you have not conceived of a hand that is an attribute and a face that is an attribute without being a body part?' It is said to him: That is not necessary, just as it is not necessary, when we have not conceived of a living, knowing, powerful being except as a body, that we (both you and we) should judge Allah (ta'ala) by that. And just as it is not necessary, when something is self-subsistent (qa'im bi-dhatihi), that it be a substance or a body, because we (both you and we) have not found a self-subsistent being in our witnessed world except as such.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage presents additional evidence for the refutation and then answers an objection. First, Baqillani argues that if 'yad' only meant power or blessing, Iblis would have used that argument when refusing to prostrate to Adam: he could have said 'I too was created by Your power and blessing, so why should I prostrate to Adam?' But Iblis did not say that, and the Qur'an records his objection differently. Moreover, the fact that Allah favored Adam by creating him 'with His two hands' (bi-yadayhi) shows that this phrase signifies a special honor, which would be lost if it only meant power or blessing. Then an objector raises a common problem: how can you affirm that Allah has a hand and a face without these being physical body parts (jarha), since we only know hands and faces as body parts? Baqillani's answer is twofold. First, the argument from analogy does not bind us; we do not limit Allah to what we experience. Just as we affirm that Allah is living, knowing, and powerful without being a body (though we only know such attributes in embodied beings), we can affirm hand and face as non-corporeal attributes. Second, we also affirm that Allah is self-subsistent (qa'im bi-dhatihi) without being a substance or body, even though in the witnessed world every self-subsistent entity is a substance or body. Therefore, the fact that we have no example of a non-corporeal hand or face does not prove they cannot exist as divine attributes.

يد صفة (hand as attribute)
وجه صفة (face as attribute)
جارحة (body part)
قياس الغائب على الشاهد (analogy from the unseen to the witnessed)
إبليس (Iblis)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming divine attributes like 'yad' (hand) necessarily implies that Allah has physical body parts, because we only know hands as body parts.
Correction: Baqillani shows that our lack of experience with non-corporeal attributes does not make them impossible for Allah, just as we affirm His knowledge and power without bodies.

Checkpoint

B) To prove that Iblis would have used the metaphorical interpretation to his advantage if it were true.

D) To argue that Iblis was a Mu'tazilite.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses the Iblis story to prove that divine attributes like 'hand' are not mere metaphors, and he defends non-corporeal attributes by analogizing to other divine attributes that transcend our experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah created Adam with His two hands, do you feel a deep sense of honor and closeness to your Creator, or do you instinctively try to explain it away? What does your reaction reveal about your heart's comfort with divine transcendence?
?
Iblis refused to submit because he saw himself as superior. Where in your life have you used theological reinterpretation—turning divine commands into metaphors—to avoid submitting to something you don't like? What would it cost you to accept that command as real?
?
If you truly believed that Allah's hand is real—beyond metaphor yet beyond matter—would you pray differently today? Would you fear Him more? Would you trust His power more? What keeps you from living in that reality right now?

Classification of Divine Attributes: Essential and Active
Classifies God's attributes into essential and active, listing each category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between God's essential attributes (صفات الذات) and active attributes (صفات الأفعال) as defined by Imam Baqillani.

Core Idea
God's essence attributes are eternal; His action attributes are temporal acts He brings into existence.

This passage from Imam Baqillani's Tamhid al-Awa'il provides a foundational classification of divine attributes. The author responds to an inquiry by detailing which attributes belong to God's essence and which pertain to His actions. Understanding this distinction is crucial for appreciating how Sunni theologians reconcile God's eternal descriptions with His temporal acts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own classification come through before you interpret.
The passage begins with a request for clarification, which Baqillani answers directly.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the definitions for 'attributes of essence' and 'attributes of action'. Notice how the author defines each before listing examples.
Attributes of essence are those God has always had and will always have.
3
Examine the lists
Go through the lists of attributes. Some, like 'face' and 'hands', may seem anthropomorphic. Note that Baqillani includes them as essential but non-physical attributes.
The list includes both well-known attributes (life, knowledge) and controversial ones (face, hands).
4
Understand the nuance on eternal description
Baqillani explains that God's description of Himself as 'Creator' is eternal because it is part of His eternal speech, even though the act of creation occurs in time. Grasp this subtlety.
This reconciles God's eternal attributes with temporal actions.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this classification matters: it preserves God's perfection without limiting His actions or likening Him to creation.
This classification is a cornerstone of Ash'ari theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب تفصيل صفات الذات من صفات الأفعال
فإن قال قائل: ففصّلوا لي صفات ذاته من صفات أفعاله لأعرف ذلك قيل له: صفات ذاته هي التي لم يزل ولا يزال موصوفاً بها. وهي الحياة والعلم والقدرة والسمع والبصر والكلام والإرادة والبقاء والوجه والعينان واليدان والغضب والرضى وهما الإرادة على ما وصفناه. والرحمة والسخط والولاية والعداوة والحبّ والإيثار والمشيئة وإدراكه تعالى لكل جنس يدركه الخلق من الطعوم والروائح والحرارة والبرودة وغير ذلك من المدركات. وصفات فعله الخلق والرزق والعدل والإحسان والتفضّل والإنعام والثواب والعقاب والحشر والنشر وكل صفة كان موجوداً قبل فعله لها. غير أن وصفه لنفسه ذلك قديم، لأنه كلامه بجميع الذي هو قوله: «إني خالق رازق باسط» وهو تعالى لم يزل متكلماً بكلام غير محدث ولا مخلوق.
Chapter: Detailing the attributes of essence from the attributes of action. So if someone says: 'Detail for me the attributes of His essence from the attributes of His actions so that I may know that.' It is said to him: The attributes of His essence are those with which He has never ceased and will never cease to be described. They are: life, knowledge, power, hearing, sight, speech, will, eternal duration, face, two eyes, two hands, anger, good pleasure—and they are will according to what we described—and mercy, wrath, guardianship, enmity, love, preference, will, and His perception of every kind that creatures perceive of tastes, smells, heat, cold, and other perceptibles. And the attributes of His action are: creation, provision, justice, beneficence, favor, bestowal, reward, punishment, gathering, spreading, and every attribute that existed before His act of it. However, His description of Himself with that is eternal, because it is His speech with all that which is His saying: 'Indeed I am Creator, Provider, Extender.' And He, exalted, has never ceased to be speaking with speech not originated nor created.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage classifies God's attributes into two fundamental types: attributes of essence (صفات الذات) and attributes of action (صفات الأفعال). The author begins by answering a request to distinguish between them. Attributes of essence are those that God has always possessed and will always possess; they are eternal and inseparable from His essence. He then provides a list: life, knowledge, power, hearing, sight, speech, will, eternal duration (بقاء), face, two eyes, two hands, anger, good pleasure (explaining that these two are essentially will), mercy, wrath, guardianship, enmity, love, preference, will, and God's perception of all sensory qualities. Notably, terms like 'face', 'eyes', 'hands' are included among essential attributes, understood as real but non-physical. Attributes of action are those that God brings into existence in time, such as creation, provision, justice, etc. However, the author emphasizes that God's description of Himself as 'Creator' or 'Provider' is eternal because it is part of His eternal speech (the Quran). This means the attribute of being a Creator, for example, is an eternal description even though the act of creation occurs in time. The distinction is crucial for avoiding both anthropomorphism and denying God's eternal attributes.

صفات الأفعال
البقاء

الرضى
الإرادة
الخلق
الكلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'face' and 'hands' are literal body parts, implying anthropomorphism.
Correction: The author includes them as essential attributes, understood in a manner befitting God without physicality, consistent with Sunni theology's tanzih (transcendence).

Checkpoint

C) Attributes of essence are only the seven listed by Ash'aris.
D) Attributes of action are the ones mentioned in the Quran only.

Key Takeaway
Imam Baqillani distinguishes between attributes that are eternally true of God's essence and those that describe His temporal acts, while affirming that God's descriptions of Himself are eternal.

Proof that Eternal Duration is an Attribute of Essence
Provides a rational proof that eternal duration is an essential attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that establishes eternal duration (baqa') as a distinct essential attribute of Allah, not identical to His essence.

Core Idea
Eternal duration cannot be identical to the essence, else it would be impossible.

This lesson presents a rational proof from Imam Baqillani that the attribute of eternal duration (baqa') is an attribute of Allah's essence. The proof uses a logical impossibility: if duration were by the essence itself, it would require the impossible scenario of something enduring in the moment of its origination. This establishes the need for a distinct attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the flow of the argument: question, premise, analogy, conclusion.
Notice how the proof begins with a hypothetical objection.
2
Identify the key logical steps
Break down the argument: (1) God is eternal, (2) created things need an attribute for duration, (3) if God's duration were by essence, He would be enduring during origination which is impossible, so (4) God has an attribute of duration.
The proof relies on the impossibility of simultaneity of origination and duration.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does this show duration is an attribute of essence and not of action? Because it is a permanent attribute, not temporary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب البقاء من صفات ذاته
فإن قال قائل: وما الدليل على أن البقاء من صفات ذاته؟ قلنا: من قبل أنه لم يزل باقياً، إذ كان كائناً من غير حدوث، والباقي منا لا يكون باقياً إلا ببقاء دليل ذلك استحالة بقاء الشيء في حال حدوثه. فلو بقي لنفسه، كان باقياً في حال حدوثه، وذلك محال باتفاق. فصح أنه باقٍ ببقاء، إذ كان قديماً يستحيل أن تكون ذاته بقاءً أو في معنى الصفات.
Chapter: The eternal duration is among the attributes of His essence. So if someone says: 'What is the evidence that eternal duration is among the attributes of His essence?' We say: Because He has never ceased to be eternal, since He was existing without origination, and the eternal among us is not eternal except by an eternal duration. The evidence for that is the impossibility of a thing's remaining in the state of its origination. For if it remained by itself, it would be eternal in the state of its origination, and that is impossible by consensus. So it is established that He is eternal by an eternal duration, since He is preeternal, and it is impossible that His essence be eternal duration or in the meaning of attributes.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage provides a rational proof that the attribute of eternal duration (البقاء) is an attribute of God's essence, not an attribute of action. The proof begins with the premise that God has never ceased to be eternal (لم يزل باقياً) because He has existed without origination. The author then draws an analogy from created beings: in our experience, a thing that remains (باقٍ) does so only by means of an attribute of duration (بقاء). Why? Because we observe that something cannot persist in the very moment it begins to exist—origination and duration are mutually exclusive. If a thing were to remain by its own essence, it would be enduring in the state of its origination, which is impossible. By consensus (اتفاق), this is impossible. Therefore, God, being preeternal (قديم) and not originated, must have an attribute of eternal duration that is distinct from His essence. The author concludes that it is impossible for God's essence itself to be the attribute of duration or to be equivalent to the meaning of the attributes (i.e., the essence and attributes are distinct). This argument establishes that eternal duration is an essential, eternal attribute, not a contingent one.

Key Terms
البقاء
قديم
حدوث
ذات
باقٍ
صفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's eternal duration is identical to His essence, making it not a real attribute.
Correction: This proof shows that eternal duration is a distinct attribute because if it were identical, the impossibility of endurance during origination would apply.

Checkpoint
What is the key impossibility used in the proof?
A) Origination and duration cannot coexist in the same moment.
B) God cannot have attributes.
C) Created beings can be eternal.
D) The essence cannot be known.

Key Takeaway
Eternal duration is a distinct essential attribute of Allah, proven by the impossibility of self-subsisting duration during origination.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you reflect on the impossibility of self-subsisting duration, does it humble you to realize that even your own persistence is a gift from Allah? What changes in your gratitude today?
?
When you contemplate that Allah's eternity is not just a fact but an attribute, does it stir in you a deeper awe? Are you living as if you truly believe He has always been and always will be, or do you act as if this world is permanent?
